You have always taken on fixable projects and done a great job. Unfortunately, with carbon patchwork the result can never truly be repaired. Carbon Fiber relies upon two-factor strength (inter and intra-laminer) due to tensile properties combined with layering. You will be able to make the repair look good, but that area will never contribute to a load ever again. For example, imagine a fiberglass surfboard that has broken in half and then repaired. It will always break in the same spot. Love the channel!

Hi Matt, This will be a tricky repair especially with no access to the McLaren automotive ply 3d and ply book as we have no idea what type of resin system or prepreg carbon is used. I would be very surprised if they will ever approve any repair not drawn by their Design Office but you never know. I think your best bet would be to strip it back, have it Ultrasonically NDT tested for delamination's and have an experienced F1 contract composite design Engineer take a look. Well guys. I used to work for a carbon/glass fiber factory in Holland and we produced the front Mercedes/McLaren crash cones. Those are braided parts, so they are not repairable!. That carbon tub repair is gonna be hard with it being on the sill as that an area where the tub is usually the stiffest and strongest to protect the driver and to provide the needed torsion stiffness a car of that performance needs.  Gonna have to cut out and sand back all the damaged carbon (which is going to messy and itchy if you dont wear proper PPE), mold the sill, create a new carbon skin off that mold matching what the original tub had in terms of layup, and then bond it back to the tub with probably some overlap to ensure it still is strong and stiff enough.  It's not gonna match what McLaren originally did since they use a RTM process for making their carbon tubs but you can surely make it work. Tavarish luckily had damage on a flat section which made it cake walk with respect to a sill being damaged.

Hi Mat,  I really enjoy your videos and your channel. Your attitude, genuineness and positivity is valuable, and it's something I come for when launching your videos. Regarding Mclaren I do not agree with the idea of rebuilding something that Manufacturer denied doing. They have their reasons which is safety. They make these cars with crazy precision to master on tracks and roads.
